<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">PREVIEW-Bank of England seen holding fire on rates in Jan  </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>BY</b> </td><td>By Christina Fincher  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>434 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>9 January 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>15:38</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">LONDON, Jan 9 (Reuters) - Britain's central bank is set to leave interest rates on hold this week but a robust housing market and sizzling services sector mean higher borrowing costs may not be far off.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The Bank of England raised interest rates twice in the second half of 2006 and money markets show investors think another quarter percentage point increase -- to 5.25 percent -- is likely in February.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Annual inflation has been above target for more than six months and accelerated to 2.7 percent in November, its highest since comparable records began a decade ago.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Policymakers are concerned that rising living costs will trigger inflationary wage deals in the New Year pay round, particularly as companies appear to be scrambling over themselves to attract new workers.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">A survey last week showed British service sector companies took on employees last month at the fastest rate in more than nine years as the sector -- which covers everything from banks to cafes -- grew at its fastest rate in nearly a decade.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"While pressure for a further rise in interest rates has recently mounted, it is still odds-on that the Bank of England will keep interest rates unchanged," said Howard Archer, economist at Global Insight. "Crucially, there is not yet a clear picture of whether or not wage settlements are moving significantly higher in the early 2007 pay rounds."  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">TIMING QUESTIONS  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">History shows the Bank of England has preferred to change interest rates to coincide with its quarterly inflation forecasts, published in February, May, August and November.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"Most economic releases have surprised to the upside but expectations are the Bank will stay on hold till February when it can justify higher interest rates with new inflation forecasts," said Andy Chaytor, rates strategist at RBS Financial Markets.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Minutes of December's rate-setting meeting showed policymakers were also concerned that the full impact of the recent monetary tightening had yet to be felt.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Sterling's recent rise to a six-year high on a trade-weighted index may also make the bank more reluctant to raise interest rates. By dampening import price inflation, a stronger pound works to tighten monetary conditions.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">A poll of economists last week showed a 45 percent chance the Bank will raise interest rates in February. Futures markets are more hawkish with prices fully discounting rates of 5.25 percent this quarter and reflecting a good chance that rates will rise to 5.5 percent by mid-year.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />BRITAIN-RATES/PREVIEW|LANGEN|ABX|BNX|FUN</td></tr>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">WRAPUP 1-UK Christmas sales up but tough times seen ahead  </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>BY</b> </td><td>By Matt Falloon  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>503 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>9 January 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>13:53</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">LONDON, Jan 9 (Reuters) - Spending in Britain accelerated at Christmas, according to a survey on Tuesday, but analysts said the prospect of yet higher interest rates will quell any lingering hopes of a blockbuster year ahead for the consumer.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The British Retail Consortium said retail sales growth picked up in December, scotching predictions of Christmas woe for shops, and high street icon Marks &amp; Spencer reported sales rose over the festive period.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Yet Marks &amp; Spencer chief executive Stuart Rose warned rising interest rates and household bills made for an uncertain outlook and he predicted "belt-tightening" ahead.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Economists say that is likely to become a familiar phrase in the coming months.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"The retail sector overall seems to have performed somewhat better over the festive period than was anticipated," said George Buckley, an economist at Deutsche Bank. "Still, that does not guarantee such conditions will last."  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Money markets have priced in an interest rate rise to 5.25 percent next month and a growing number of analysts also say the Bank of England will repeat its August and November quarter point increases as it seeks to tame above-target inflation.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">By that time, the Bank will have some indication of how the higher cost of living is seeping through to inflationary wage demands -- a scenario policymakers are keen to avoid -- following the key New Year pay round.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">WAGE WAR  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Demand for staff is strong, according to the Recruitment and Employment Confederation, which said staffing agencies placed workers in permanent positions last month at the fastest rate in nearly three years.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">That would imply higher wage inflation and the survey showed wage growth close to November's 71-month high.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Economists say concerns are also growing about the robust health of the housing market -- where most surveys point to strong price growth and demand despite higher borrowing costs.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Companies that make their money in housing -- house builders including Bovis and property agents such as Savills -- are reporting upbeat results to back up the data.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">But higher profits at Savills, an upmarket adviser, also reflect a gulf of affordability in the housing market where London prices are soaring faster than elsewhere and new buyers across the country are struggling to afford a home.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">If the BoE does hike rates in February, more and more first-time buyers will be unable to get a foot on the property ladder and those who dared to spend at Christmas may not feel so eager to return and more, analysts say.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"We continue to believe that the upside for consumer spending will be limited during much of 2007," said Howard Archer, an economist at Global Insight.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"This is due to the major headwinds that consumers face -- higher interest rates, elevated utility bills, moderate real earnings growth, an increasing tax burden, rising debt levels and pension concerns."  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />BRITAIN-ECONOMY/ (WRAPUP 1)|LANGEN|ABN|M|E|RBN|D|UKR|RWS|BNX|UKI|RNP|DNP</td></tr>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">TABLE-How British retailers fared over Christmas  </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>614 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>9 January 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>13:37</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">LONDON, Jan 9 (Reuters) - British retailers had a bumpy ride in the crucial Christmas trading season as unseasonably warm weather, rate hikes and tame wage growth led to low shopper turnout and profit warnings at some mid-market stores.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">With the full picture of the festive shopping period not expected to be clear for several weeks, analysts predict the winners to be luxury goods sellers, online stores, premium grocers and Britain's biggest retailer, Tesco , which is expected to provide a trading statement next week.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Following is a list of trading updates from retailers following the festive rush. All figures are year-on-year and compare same store sales unless otherwise stated.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">COMPANY COMMENT  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">(* denotes new addition)  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">ALEXON Like-for-like sales fell 4 percent in the 22 weeks to Dec. 30, while margins were 1 percent lower, reflecting greater markdown activity.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">AQUASCUTUM Total sales at the luxury wear stores were up 32 to 33 percent in the eight weeks to mid-December.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">ASDA Said on Jan. 4 that sales during the Christmas trading spell were better than expected.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">CLINTON CARDS Like-for-like sales at its high street stores rose 1.8 percent in the five weeks before Christmas, with strong growth in cards blunted by gift sales.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">*COOPERATIVE GROUP Like-for-like sales in the 13 weeks to Jan. 6 rose 6.1 percent.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">DEBENHAMS Warned on Dec. 12 that tough trading conditions had made for worsening sales since the start of September.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">*DUNELM Like-for-like sales in the six months to Dec. 30 rose 5 percent, with second quarter sales up 5.8 percent.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">GAMES WORKSHOP Warned full-year profit was likely to fall short, because in-line Christmas sales would not make up for a poor summer.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"></p><pre class="articlePre">  
 GREETINGS CARD GROUP      Filed for administration Jan. 2.
 
 *HALFORDS GROUP           Said on Jan. 9 that trading since Nov. 23 had been
in line with its expectations.
 
 HARVEY NICHOLS            Sales in its luxury department stores were up by
"mid-double digits" in the run-up to Christmas.
 
 HMV                       Warned on Dec. 20 that profit was likely to come
in at the bottom of expectations.

 HOUSE OF FRASER           Like-for-like sales rose 7.3 percent in the four
weeks to Dec. 30, with record trading in the week before Christmas.
 
 JESSOPS                   Like-for-like sales were down 6.9 percent in the
six weeks to Jan 5 and down 1.9 percent in the 14 weeks to the same date. Market
softness and tough comparatives with last year were to blame.
 
 JOHN LEWIS                Total group sales for the week ended Dec. 30 rose
9.6 percent year-on-year.
 
 LIBERTY                   Sales in the four weeks to Christmas rose 6
percent, boosted by demand for luxury fashion accessories and fragrances for
women.
 
 MAJESTIC WINE             Sales in the last nine weeks of 2006 rose 4.4
  </pre>
<p></p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">percent.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">*MARKS AND SPENCER UK like for like sales up 5.6 percent in the 13 weeks to Dec. 30.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"></p><pre class="articlePre"> MUSIC ZONE                Filed for administration Jan. 3.
 NEW LOOK                  Like-for-like sales rose 3.2 percent in the 14
weeks to Dec. 30, with total sales up 26 percent amid new store openings.
 
 NEXT                      Like-for-like sales at its stores fell 6.9 percent
from July 31 to Dec. 24, but total sales including the Next Directory rose 9.3
percent, and said year profit would be slightly ahead of analysts' forecasts.
 
 WOOLWORTHS                Warned on Dec. 5 its full-year profit could fall
  </pre>
<p></p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">to half of last year's total if sales did not pick up.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />RETAILERS-BRITAIN/TRADING|LANGEN|Table|ABN|E|RBN|UKI|M|D</td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>IN</b> </td><td><br />i64 : Retail/Wholesale | iint : Internet/Online Services</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>NS</b> </td><td><br />e11 : Economic Performance/Indicators | mcat : Commodity/Financial Market News | ntab : Table | ecat : Economic News | ncat : Content Types | nfact : Factiva Filters | nfce : FC&amp;E Exclusion Filter | niwe : IWE Filter</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RE</b> </td><td><br />eurz : Europe | uk : United Kingdom | weurz : Western Europe | eecz : European Union Countries</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>IPC</b> </td><td><br />RET | MCE | ECI | WWW | CPX</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>PUB</b> </td><td><br />Reuters Limited</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>AN</b> </td><td><br />Document LBA0000020070109e31900110</td></tr></tbody></table><br /></div>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">Investors scramble for UK 20-year gilts  </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>287 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>9 January 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>12:32</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">LONDON, Jan 9 (Reuters) - Investors lapped up Britain's first gilt auction of 2007 on Tuesday, bidding more than twice as much as the 2.25 billion pounds of 2027 securities on offer.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The Debt Management Office said it sold the paper at an average yield of 4.413 percent and a bid to cover ratio of 2.3.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">That was much higher than the 1.51 cover at the last sale of the 4.25 percent securities in December, when the same amount was sold at a yield of 4.218 percent.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The strong result reverberated in the gilt market, propelling March futures to stand a fifth of a point higher on the day, while 10-year cash yields fell 3 basis points. Analysts had expected the sale to fare well as yields on the securities were trading much higher than at earlier taps, meaning the paper represented good value for investors. However, they were still surprised by the strength of demand. Strategists said pension funds seemed to have turned out in force at Tuesday's sale, noting that long-dated gilts had been supported by such investors since the end of December, possibly to avoid being caught short in the event of a rally.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"This time we're seeing a participation of real money investors not wanting to go underweight on the long end just in case we get a repeat of last year," said Francis Diamond, strategist at JP Morgan.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Pension funds need to hold long-dated gilts on their books to match the payments they will have to make in years to come.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />MARKETS-BRITAIN-AUCTION (URGENT)|LANGEN|ABN|M|D|UKI|DNP</td></tr>
